package org.apache.commons.pool2.impl;
18
19 
import java.io.Serializable;
20 
import java.util.AbstractQueue;
21 
import java.util.Collection;
22 
import java.util.Deque;
23

/**
30 
 * An optionally-bounded {@linkplain java.util.concurrent.BlockingDeque blocking
31 
 * deque} based on linked nodes.
32 
 *
33 
 * <p> The optional capacity bound constructor argument serves as a
34 
 * way to prevent excessive expansion. The capacity, if unspecified,
35 
 * is equal to {@link Integer#MAX_VALUE}.  Linked nodes are
36 
 * dynamically created upon each insertion unless this would bring the
37 
 * deque above capacity.
38 
 * </p>
39 
 *
40 
 * <p>Most operations run in constant time (ignoring time spent
41 
 * blocking).  Exceptions include {@link #remove(Object) remove},
42 
 * {@link #removeFirstOccurrence removeFirstOccurrence}, {@link
43 
 * #removeLastOccurrence removeLastOccurrence}, {@link #contains
44 
 * contains}, {@link #iterator iterator.remove()}, and the bulk
45 
 * operations, all of which run in linear time.
46 
 * </p>
47 
 *
48 
 * <p>This class and its iterator implement all of the
49 
 * <em>optional</em> methods of the {@link Collection} and {@link
50 
 * Iterator} interfaces.
51 
 * </p>
52 
 *
53 
 * <p>This class is a member of the
54 
 * <a href="{@docRoot}/../technotes/guides/collections/index.html">
55 
 * Java Collections Framework</a>.
56 
 * </p>
57 
 *
58 
 * @param <E> the type of elements held in this collection
59 
 *
60 
 * Note: This was copied from Apache Harmony and modified to suit the needs of
61 
 *       Commons Pool.
62 
 *
63 
 * @since 2.0
64 
 */
65 
class LinkedBlockingDeque<E> extends AbstractQueue<E>
66 
        implements Deque<E>, Serializable {
67
68 
    /*
69 
     * Implemented as a simple doubly-linked list protected by a
70 
     * single lock and using conditions to manage blocking.
71 
     *
72 
     * To implement weakly consistent iterators, it appears we need to
73 
     * keep all Nodes GC-reachable from a predecessor dequeued Node.
74 
     * That would cause two problems:
75 
     * - allow a rogue Iterator to cause unbounded memory retention
76 
     * - cause cross-generational linking of old Nodes to new Nodes if
77 
     *   a Node was tenured while live, which generational GCs have a
78 
     *   hard time dealing with, causing repeated major collections.
79 
     * However, only non-deleted Nodes need to be reachable from
80 
     * dequeued Nodes, and reachability does not necessarily have to
81 
     * be of the kind understood by the GC.  We use the trick of
82 
     * linking a Node that has just been dequeued to itself.  Such a
83 
     * self-link implicitly means to jump to "first" (for next links)
84 
     * or "last" (for prev links).
85 
     */
86
87 
    /*
88 
     * We have "diamond" multiple interface/abstract class inheritance
89 
     * here, and that introduces ambiguities. Often we want the
90 
     * BlockingDeque javadoc combined with the AbstractQueue
91 
     * implementation, so a lot of method specs are duplicated here.
92 
     */
93
94 
    private static final long serialVersionUID = -387911632671998426L;
95
96 
    /**
97 
     * Doubly-linked list node class.
98 
     *
99 
     * @param <E> node item type
100 
     */
101 
    private static final class Node<E> {
102 
        /**
103 
         * The item, or null if this node has been removed.
104 
         */
105 
        E item;
106
107 
        /**
108 
         * One of:
109 
         * - the real predecessor Node
110 
         * - this Node, meaning the predecessor is tail
111 
         * - null, meaning there is no predecessor
112 
         */
113 
        Node<E> prev;
114
115 
        /**
116 
         * One of:
117 
         * - the real successor Node
118 
         * - this Node, meaning the successor is head
119 
         * - null, meaning there is no successor
120 
         */
121 
        Node<E> next;
122
123 
        /**
124 
         * Create a new list node.
125 
         *
126 
         * @param x The list item
127 
         * @param p Previous item
128 
         * @param n Next item
129 
         */
130 
        Node(final E x, final Node<E> p, final Node<E> n) {
131 
            item = x;
132 
            prev = p;
133 
            next = n;
134 
        }
135 
    }
136
137 
    /**
138 
     * Pointer to first node.
139 
     * Invariant: (first == null && last == null) ||
140 
     *            (first.prev == null && first.item != null)
141 
     */
142 
    private transient Node<E> first; // @GuardedBy("lock")
143
144 
    /**
145 
     * Pointer to last node.
146 
     * Invariant: (first == null && last == null) ||
147 
     *            (last.next == null && last.item != null)
148 
     */
149 
    private transient Node<E> last; // @GuardedBy("lock")
150
151 
    /** Number of items in the deque */
152 
    private transient int count; // @GuardedBy("lock")
153
154 
    /** Maximum number of items in the deque */
155 
    private final int capacity;
156
157 
    /** Main lock guarding all access */
158 
    private final InterruptibleReentrantLock lock;
159
160 
    /** Condition for waiting takes */
161 
    private final Condition notEmpty;
162
163 
    /** Condition for waiting puts */
164 
    private final Condition notFull;
165
